  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_372b1a49-626e-4636-a4e3-5c8df862baab'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText11761809235928650138" style="display:none"><b>Raw, captivating, and undeniably real, Nic Stone joins industry giants Jason Reynolds and Walter Dean Myers as she boldly tackles American race relations in this stunning debut.</b><br /><br />Justyce McAllister is top of his class and set for the Ivy League—but none of that matters to the police officer who just put him in handcuffs. And despite leaving his rough neighborhood behind, he can't escape the scorn of his former peers or the ridicule of his new classmates. Justyce looks to the teachings of Dr. Martin Luther King Jr. for answers. But do they hold up anymore? He starts a journal to Dr. King to find out.<br /><br />Then comes the day Justyce goes driving with his best friend, Manny, windows rolled down, music turned up—way up, sparking the fury of a white off-duty cop beside them. Words fly. Shots are fired. Justyce and Manny are caught in the crosshairs. In the media fallout, it's Justyce who is under attack.</span>

It recommends this book for grade<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">As a school librarian, I have found that School Library Journal is generally on spot with age/grade recommendations. It recommends this book for grades 9 and up. I would recommend to grades 8 and up due to mature language, and topics. Characters are high school seniors and I generally keep the the character age close to age of reader. Excellent book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33982178-dear-martin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1866606187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1574381543782166771">For some, it sounds like the kind of dystopian world inspired by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a>. A dark, dystopian future where young men are <b>gunned down for doing nothing wrong</b>. Imagine trying to live your life with the constant knowledge that you could be murdered for… wearing the wrong clothes… looking “shady”… or having the wrong colour skin. Imagine living this nightmare and STILL being told that it doesn’t happen anymore. That everyone is equal and, actually, YOU are given an advantage by affirmative ac</span>
  <span id="freeText1574381543782166771" style="display:none">For some, it sounds like the kind of dystopian world inspired by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. A dark, dystopian future where young men are <b>gunned down for doing nothing wrong</b>. Imagine trying to live your life with the constant knowledge that you could be murdered for… wearing the wrong clothes… looking “shady”… or having the wrong colour skin. Imagine living this nightmare and STILL being told that it doesn’t happen anymore. That everyone is equal and, actually, YOU are given an advantage by affirmative action programs. <br /><br /><b>But this isn’t a dark dystopia. It’s the world we live in</b>. Maybe it’s not a world I am forced to deal with. Or you. Or you over there. But it’s the world many black Americans face every day.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24974996.Dear_Martin" title="Dear Martin by Nic Stone" rel="nofollow noopener">Dear Martin</a> introduces us to Justyce - a strong and important voice in YA. There are so few YA books with POC narrators and especially lacking are those with non-white teen boys, so this book is particularly needed. Through third person narration alternating with Justyce's letters to Martin Luthor King Jr., we get insight into some of the experiences had by black teenage boys.<br /><br />For those looking for books to complement <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give" title="The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a>, this is a good place to start. While <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give" title="The Hate U Give by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a> looks at the shooting of unarmed black men and boys through the eyes of a female witness, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24974996.Dear_Martin" title="Dear Martin by Nic Stone" rel="nofollow noopener">Dear Martin</a> instead offers what it is like to be one of those racially-profiled black men. <br /><br />It is not just about shooting, though. This book explores smaller but deeply hurtful acts of racially-charged aggression, such as the anger held by white students over affirmative action programs. Or the demand to "stop being so sensitive" in the face of race-related jokes. It is especially interesting when the author also considers the animosity Justyce receives from the black boys in his neighbourhood. He finds himself torn between the need to be true to his roots and his desire to succeed in a world that demands he play the white man's game to get ahead. <br /><br />All that being said, <b>it's not a perfect book</b>. While many complex issues are considered, some aspects are simplistic and lacking in nuance. Justyce is an unquestionably nice, well-mannered boy who wants to follow in the “moral high ground” footsteps of MLK. While it is important to deconstruct the aggressive thug stereotype associated with young black men, teens this mild-mannered and uncomplicated are hard to believe in. I was a shy bookworm and even I had more bite than Justyce.<br /><br />In contrast, all of the racism is very overt. The cops all stomp around punching black guys in the face and using the n-word, while Justyce's white classmates are so stupidly and openly racist to the point where one of them thinks it's funny to go to a party dressed as a Ku Klux Klan member. Does this level of abhorrent behaviour happen? Absolutely! But the real problem we face today is more insidious, more subtle, hiding behind a "I just feared for my life, your honour". In reality, it is much more complex than good vs. bad where the bad wears a white hood and shouts racist insults. That is why young black men are so at risk and their murderers so likely to escape justice - because the most dangerous racists no longer wear the t-shirt.<br /><br />I would have also liked to see <b>more of a challenge to the misogyny</b>. I wouldn't say it's glorified, but it is never addressed when Manny, a black boy, says he dislikes black girls because he’s never met any that aren’t ghetto and full of attitude. Seems like a strange message to send out in a book of this kind.<br /><br />But the good definitely outweighs the bad. Problems aside, this is a short, quick read that packs a huge punch. I feel like I'll be thinking about it for a long time.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1574381543782166771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2091898748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091898748" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2091898748?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091898748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3887305184131719094"><b>NOTE: As a white woman, I am incapable of fully understanding the issues that plague black individuals today. I recognize my privilege and try to learn something new every single day, and I am so grateful for authors like Nic Stone who can teach me new ways of seeing society. That said, my opinion on this book is honestly so much less important than own-voice reviewers' words. <u>If you or someone you know is an own-voice reviewer of this book and would like your review to be featured in my blog po</u></b></span>
  <span id="freeText3887305184131719094" style="display:none"><b>NOTE: As a white woman, I am incapable of fully understanding the issues that plague black individuals today. I recognize my privilege and try to learn something new every single day, and I am so grateful for authors like Nic Stone who can teach me new ways of seeing society. That said, my opinion on this book is honestly so much less important than own-voice reviewers' words. <u>If you or someone you know is an own-voice reviewer of this book and would like your review to be featured in my blog post, please message me here on Goodreads or DM me on twitter because I would love to share your words.</u></b><br /><br />First and foremost, let me tell you that this is one of the most <i>
  <b>important</b>
</i> stories that I have ever had the mixed pleasure and heartache of reading. Justyce's story is one of societal racism, police brutality, toxic masculinity, and privilege. His letters to Martin Luther King, Jr. beautifully depict the pain and difficulty that comes with being a black individual in the United States today.<br /><br />It is so incredibly intersectional and finds a way to address so many talking points that many of my peers - of all ages - could benefit from seeing through this book's lens. No matter your political stance, I would highly encourage every single person to pick up a copy of <i>Dear Martin</i> and go into it with your eyes and mind as wide open as possible.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"How do I work against this, Martin? Getting real with you, I feel a little defeated. Knowing there are people who don't want me to succeed is depressing. Especially coming from two directions."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Something exceptionally interesting to me about Nic Stone's writing in this book is her decision to address not only racism, but also the mindset that some individuals in the black community have regarding themselves and other POC. There is a lot of explanation given for how, in a nutshell, once a group of people have been put down over and over for so long, in such painful ways, and have been shown that no amount of effort they can put forth will be recognized as equal, it can be easy to feel defeated and hopeless - sometimes to the point of giving up.<br /><br />Justyce's reaction to his unlawful arrest, and the ways that his privileged, wealthy white classmates treat him, broke my heart. He becomes so hopeless at times. Despite being incredibly brilliant and hard-working, Jus questions his own worth at points, asking, "Am I ever going to get anywhere? Is this battle worth fighting?"<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Do I just take what they dish out, try to stop being "so sensitive"? What do I do when my very identity is being mocked by people who refuse to admit there's a problem?"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />What may have been the most painful aspect of reading <i>Dear Martin</i> for me, was watching the way his so-called "friends" treated him. The microaggressions escalated steadily to blatant cruelty, and so much of it looked so familiar to things <i>I</i> saw and heard people say firsthand, growing up in the Atlanta metro. I'm so ashamed to say this, but there were even comments that I remembered making similar assumptions to as a young teen, and seeing it on paper like that brutally reminded me of how many people <i>I</i> have hurt with my carelessness in years past.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"My dudes... they're like family to me. They've got my back as long as I have theirs."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />One of many topics Nic Stone handled beautifully was the portrayal of gangs, and the reasoning for why so many teens get sucked into them: at the root of many gangs lies a family, something to hold on to and to protect yourself with. In a society that has ceaselessly attacked the individuals it deems "other", is it any surprise that individuals like Justyce's childhood friend would seek solace in gangs?<br /><br />The entire gang discussion in <i>Dear Martin</i> also highlights some serious struggles with toxic masculinity and the way it can effect young people in particular, leading young men to believe that proving their worth means violence, aggression, etc. While it's not a topic that is focused on very clearly in this book, it's worth mentioning.<br /><br />Among other less-discussed topics in the book, there's time taken to dive into sexism (like Justyce's frequent remarks to Manny that he is "such a girl", which is later challenged), misogynoir and internalized racism (as Justyce's best friend, Manny, admits that he struggles to find black women attractive, and goes on to categorize them stereotypically and unfairly), and discrimination and how it can impact both sides (Justyce has a crush on his best friend - a Jewish girl named SJ - but refuses to pursue it due to his mother's insistence that no black son of hers should have anything to do with a white girl).<br /><br />There's also a heavy line of discussion about police brutality, which we get to see somewhat from both sides: Justyce wonders if one cop's racism is influenced by having seen his partner shot by a black teen months prior - blame is never 100% placed on either side, and nobody's actions are justified. As a result of police brutality, Justyce's best friend's father joins a protest group (seemingly similar to Black Lives Matter), and is forced to resign from his management position as a result of being seen with "those people". I know that BLM and police brutality is a hot topic of controversy here in the states lately, and I thought Nic Stone made her points flawlessly.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"In that moment, when I thought I was dying, it hit me: despite how good of a dude Martin was, they still killed him, man."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />This quote in particular was what finally broke me in <i>Dear Martin</i>. I have grown so weary of individuals claiming that marginalized groups - particularly black individuals - don't protest "the right way". If they stand silent, it's wrong. If they kneel, it's wrong. If they wear t-shirts and hold signs, it's wrong. This is so incredibly relevant to the turmoil facing our nation today, and at a certain point, you <i>have</i> to wake up and realize: <b>it isn't about the protests - it never was. It's about the skin color of the protesters.</b><br /><br />I feel like there's so much more that I could say about <i>Dear Martin</i>. I'm sitting here with tears streaking down my cheeks, and all I want to do is say any combination of the right words to convince you to pick this book up, to lose yourself in this story the way I did. To go into it with open eyes and to <i>learn something</i> from Nic Stone's experiences. If there could ever be a contemporary title that I could convince you to get a copy of, let it be <i>Dear Martin.</i><br /><br /><b>Content warnings:</b> racism, police brutality, violence, death, misogyny/misogynoir.<br /><br /><i>All quotes are taken from an ARC. Thank you so much to PRH/CROWN for sending me this ARC in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2017/10/18/dear-martin/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3887305184131719094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1932942052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1932942052" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1932942052?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1932942052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15297299763390164066">5/5 Stars! LOVED THIS BOOK SO MUCH.<br/><br/>CW: racism, police brutality<br/><br/><i>Dear Martin</i> had me captivated the entire time, I seriously could not put it down. I finished it in under 3 hours so if you are looking for a short yet intense read, this is the one for you!<br/><br/>I feel I avoided <i>Dear Martin</i> for a few months because I assumed the entire novel was written in letters to Dr. King, which is not a format I prefer to read. I was pleasantly surprised to find the letters complimented the chronological storytelling,</span>
  <span id="freeText15297299763390164066" style="display:none">5/5 Stars! LOVED THIS BOOK SO MUCH.<br /><br />CW: racism, police brutality<br /><br /><i>Dear Martin</i> had me captivated the entire time, I seriously could not put it down. I finished it in under 3 hours so if you are looking for a short yet intense read, this is the one for you!<br /><br />I feel I avoided <i>Dear Martin</i> for a few months because I assumed the entire novel was written in letters to Dr. King, which is not a format I prefer to read. I was pleasantly surprised to find the letters complimented the chronological storytelling, and was a great addition in my opinion. I feel Justyce’s story would be incomplete without a place to share his unfiltered thoughts with a figure he aims to emulate.<br /><br /><i>Dear Martin</i> does not shy away from much-needed conversations about racism and racial profiling in America, but it also delves into conversations about toxic masculinity and gangs. I feel this novel successfully accomplishes approaching these tough issues by displaying a variety of perspectives. These discussions are raw, uncensored, and full of truth we cannot turn a blind eye to.<br /><br />I also loved that while this book deals with serious topics, the character dynamics do often bring enough humor to the story to balance out the intensity. I thoroughly enjoyed Justyce’s narration – It was so satisfying to read from the perspective of an intelligent, self/socially aware teen.<br /><br />All together, I loved <i>Dear Martin</i>. I think my only critique is attributed to the fact that I wish it was longer! I would have loved more scenes, more letters to Dr. King, more development from side characters. Otherwise, it was a really fantastic read I would definitely recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15297299763390164066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1838270389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1838270389" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1838270389?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1838270389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4516045292246766005"><b>This was super brutal and super good!</b> And so <i>smol</i>...it literally arrived in the mail and I nearly lost it in the packaging. But while I do have some quibbles about the size, ultimately I think it's AMAZING that 200 pages can pack this massive punch. <b>This is the kind of #BlackLivesMatter book that's super important for everyone to read.</b> And as the author's note says, it's: <i>"...an attempt to examine current affairs through the lens of Rev. Dr. Martin Luther King Jr.'s teachings."</i> Which was SO grea</span>
  <span id="freeText4516045292246766005" style="display:none"><b>This was super brutal and super good!</b> And so <i>smol</i>...it literally arrived in the mail and I nearly lost it in the packaging. But while I do have some quibbles about the size, ultimately I think it's AMAZING that 200 pages can pack this massive punch. <b>This is the kind of #BlackLivesMatter book that's super important for everyone to read.</b> And as the author's note says, it's: <i>"...an attempt to examine current affairs through the lens of Rev. Dr. Martin Luther King Jr.'s teachings."</i> Which was SO great to read and learn about.<br /><br /><b>I also really adored Justyce!</b> He's like just doing his best and he's super smart and the world just kicks him down. I also liked how he's on the brink of graduation, because it's really nice reading about teens who know what they're doing (HE'S GOING TO YALE) and are off to like change the world. Like, go Justyce. I really admire this dude.<br /><br /><b>It's of course not an "easy" story either.</b> It's going to thump you in the feels. And the court case scene totally blew me away with how unfair and tangled it was...but like the <i>writing</i>. This book is full of intelligence and it's super well written!<br /><br /><b>ALOS IT'S WRITTEN IN 3RD PERSON / PRESENT TENSE WHICH IS MY FAVOURITE.</b> You know how hard it is to find books in this style?!? I'm happpppy.<br /><br /><b>OK so the ONLY quibble I have is that --&gt; being so short, it was hard to SEE everything.</b> I missed out on all the details, the mannerisms, the facial quirks, the smells and sights and tastes. The book is probably 80% straight dialogue? (Often in like a screen-writing format.) So I LIKED that, but (for me personally) I prefer writing that fleshes out the world as well. This also made a lot of the secondary characters are to "get to know" because we just see their dialogue and that's it.<br /><br />But hey. I love dialogue also!!<br /><br /><b>Definitely an important narrative that can't be talked about enough.</b> The world needs to change and I'm so glad #ownvoices authors are putting their stories out there to make a difference. It tackles racism and classism head on and it's full of unfairness and character development and letters and hope. &lt;3<br /><br /><blockquote>"You ever consider that maybe you not supposed to 'fit'? People who make history rarely do."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4516045292246766005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1991719274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1991719274" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991719274?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone and everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991719274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17976786549147059028"><b>Every moment of this felt like a punch to the gut.</b> <br/><br/>There’s honestly not much else to <i>say</i> about this book. Despite being incredibly short, I think <b><i>Dear Martin</i> speaks for itself about racism</b> and hatred and prejudice. It’s hard to write a book that makes a reader <i>feel</i>, but reading this book just made me feel like I was being punched in the gut, over and over. This was just so emotionally <i>real</i>. While the characters may not get many specific traits, they all feel so much like real people. <b>It takes a </b></span>
  <span id="freeText17976786549147059028" style="display:none"><b>Every moment of this felt like a punch to the gut.</b> <br /><br />There’s honestly not much else to <i>say</i> about this book. Despite being incredibly short, I think <b><i>Dear Martin</i> speaks for itself about racism</b> and hatred and prejudice. It’s hard to write a book that makes a reader <i>feel</i>, but reading this book just made me feel like I was being punched in the gut, over and over. This was just so emotionally <i>real</i>. While the characters may not get many specific traits, they all feel so much like real people. <b>It takes a lot of talent to make characters feel so true in so few pages.</b> <br /><br />Where this book truly exceeds, though, is the thematics. I'd utterly second <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091898748" rel="nofollow noopener">my friend Destiny's words</a> as to the themes of internalized racism. What I specifically loved about this book, and something I'm not sure you'll <i>get</i> from any other book, is the emphasis on Justyce's feeling like a <b>
  <u>political debate rather than a person.</u>
</b> Holy shit, this is the <i>realest</i> feeling as marginalized person. It's like your personhood is being taken away. You are nothing but the thing that cuts you off, not to your friends, to your enemies, to your teachers. You are there to be a political pawn. You are there to be a counterexample. None of your opinions are your own - they are your group's opinions, because god forbid we think of marginalized people as anything but a monolith. There is <i>so</i> much about this here, done in a way that's sensitive and kind. I think no one put it better than Adriana @PerpetualPages in <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Lp1KgEeYlw" rel="nofollow noopener"> their review</a> - this book asks, and better yet, doesn't try to perfectly answer, whether the time for respectability politics is over. <br /><br />I feel like people are going to ignore this because of <i>The Hate U Give</i>, an equally important and fantastic book: and can I just say: <b>you shouldn't</b>. Yes, they're both <i>kind of</i> about #blacklivesmatter, but they deal with different facets of racism and in <i>completely</i> different ways. <i>The Hate U Give</i> deals with cop violence and racial profiling, yes, but I'd argue that its focus lies on how to stand up in a society filled with systematic racism. Meanwhile, <i>Dear Martin</i> focuses on toxic masculinity and the socialization of black boys in our society, the way in which they are taught they are more criminal than everyone else in some indefinable way. Both have slightly different focuses when discussing racism, both are very different books, and <b>
  <u>both are totally worth reading.</u>
</b><br /><br />It wasn't quite a five star book for me; <b>the beginning felt a little rough</b>, in particular. After a heartbreaking and near-perfect first couple chapters, the middle section is meditative and dialogue-full with a romance that feels somewhat bland. But in the end, it all works to the book's advantage. <b>The second half of this book makes everything worth it</b>. I truly felt so much towards the end. And in fact, the ending of this book is one of the best book endings I have ever read. It is so full of <i>hope</i> - hope for change, hope for continued life, hope for us to continue growing as people and as nations. A lot of the changes we can make in the future <i>need</i> to be guided along by people in positions of privilege. We need to be here. <b>It's our responsibility to support fantastic books like this that speak to the <i>importance</i> of ending racism.</b> <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17976786549147059028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2269315195" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2269315195" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2269315195?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781524782351" href="/book/show/38102513-dear-martin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2269315195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1294267413864852819"><b>Impactful. Important. Immersive.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576157482ra/28599671.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There are many different ways in which we learn about the world around us. One of the most important ways is through personal experience. These experiences help to shape our views, opinions and really who we are as people.<br/><br/>As we all know, people experience the world differently for a variety of distinct reasons. Unfortunately, one way in which this is true is based on the color of a person's skin.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576681168ra/28632328.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I know that as a white person, given the innate privileges that comes</span>
  <span id="freeText1294267413864852819" style="display:none"><b>Impactful. Important. Immersive.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576157482ra/28599671.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are many different ways in which we learn about the world around us. One of the most important ways is through personal experience. These experiences help to shape our views, opinions and really who we are as people.<br><br>As we all know, people experience the world differently for a variety of distinct reasons. Unfortunately, one way in which this is true is based on the color of a person's skin.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576681168ra/28632328.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know that as a white person, given the innate privileges that comes with, there are certain issues I will never be able to understand based on personal experience; I have to look outside of myself and my day-to-day existence if I want to acknowledge and understand certain important matters that affect so many.<br><br>That's one of the reasons why I think books such as <i>Dear Martin</i> are so crucial. That's one of the many reasons why there has been such a push, and a well-received push fortunately, for more OWN-voices books. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469047916ra/19775191.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They provide windows through the eyes of the characters, so the Reader can learn and gain knowledge from the life experiences of another.<br><br><i>Dear Martin</i> is a wonderfully written novella about a boy struggling to understand race relations within his community and his country, the United States, at large. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596591670ra/29917137.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the format of this and although some of it seemed 'surface level', as I have noticed some Readers comment, I think overall that was a wise choice by the author.<br><br>In my opinion, to make this story approachable to the widest audience, it was important to keep it this way. Not everyone is comfortable picking up a 400 or 500-page book like many of us are. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596591670ra/29917138.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think the way <i>Dear Martin</i> was written helps to get it into the hands of the largest number of people possible and for a story as important as this, that is what matters.<br><br>I highly recommend picking this one up if you haven't already. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596591670ra/29917139.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nic Stone is a very talented storyteller and I look forward to reading more of her work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1294267413864852819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2269315195">

<div id="review_2023769268" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2023769268" />
    <a title="may ➹" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68157476-may"><img alt="may ➹" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538949856p2/68157476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2023769268?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ➹" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ➹" href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=4-and-a-half-star">4-and-a-half-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-3rd">pov-3rd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=ownvoices">ownvoices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=reviews-im-proud-of">reviews-im-proud-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=rep-poc">rep-poc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023769268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18185479553088256869"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I honestly have no idea why this isn’t getting more hype, because <b>this book is absolutely beautiful, important, and poignant</b>. It opens eyes and minds about issues that are happening right now, and it offers perspective from people who are the ones facing those issues. This is a book everyone should read.<br/><br/>First, I’d like to say that I am a person of color, but I am not Black. <b>I’ve faced racism, bias, and other forms of prejudice and discrimination, but none as bad as what Black people fac</b></span>
  <span id="freeText18185479553088256869" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I honestly have no idea why this isn’t getting more hype, because <b>this book is absolutely beautiful, important, and poignant</b>. It opens eyes and minds about issues that are happening right now, and it offers perspective from people who are the ones facing those issues. This is a book everyone should read.<br /><br />First, I’d like to say that I am a person of color, but I am not Black. <b>I’ve faced racism, bias, and other forms of prejudice and discrimination, but none as bad as what Black people face.</b> So while I have had some bad experiences in that matter, it will never be on the same level as Black people have had.<br /><br />I didn’t even reach the tenth page before I got incredibly frustrated and angry, and it just continued to build over the course of the story. The events that happen in this book are horrible to read about, because they are so unjust and not something you’d ever think someone would or could experience—but <b>what makes it worse is that people <i>do</i> face these things in real life</b>. And books like these are the only way to really get just a small idea of what those people experience.<br /><br /><blockquote><i>What do I do when my very </i>identity<i> is being mocked by people who refuse to admit there’s a problem?</i></blockquote><br />Not only does this book tackle police brutality, racism, and racial profiling, however, it also covers topics such as toxic masculinity, sexism, and the “making everything about race” idea! (I sound excited when I say that, but honestly I’m just excited that a book can tackle so many things, because that is exactly what we need.)<br /><br />Justyce is a real and flawed character. His flaws make him beautiful, and they make him so much more relatable. He is kind, he is sweet, and he genuinely wants to change the way others view Black people and racial inequality. <b>I also found it so so important that he was a MOC teen narrator, and specifically Black</b>—male narrators are already scarce in YA, and MOC even scarcer. <br /><br />I also love love love the character development that Jared, your typical “There Is No Racial Inequality” White Guy, went through. In the beginning of the book, he says:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>What kind of teacher has the nerve to suggest there’s racial inequality to a classroom full of millenials?</i>
</blockquote><br />and also:<br /><br /><blockquote><i>I’m just so sick of people suggesting African Americans still have it </i>so hard<i> these days.</i></blockquote><br />and also:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>All I know is that no matter what college I end up at, when I see a minority, I’m gonna wonder if they’re qualified to be there.</i>
</blockquote><br />Obviously, all of this made me so angry, because as a white person, he cannot understand what racial inequality truly is or what Black people have gone through, because he is white. But by the end of the book, Jared realizes his privilege and works to make up for his past mistakes (even if it’s sad that that happened only when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Manny died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). And <i>that</i> is what white people should be doing, <b>working to undo the ignorance that they have had, working to recognize what privilege they have for being white, working to use that privilege to help others</b>.<br /><br />Sarah Jane (also known as SJ) was an AMAZING character and I love her so. much. <b>She is strong, smart, and will not hesitate to stand up for her opinions.</b> She is a character realizes her white privilege from the very beginning, and sticks up for forms of inequality, and also Justyce. (I also love that she apologized for “taking over” and not letting Justyce stand up for himself—because while it’s amazing that white people will defend POC, they also need to let POC speak up for themselves first, if they want to.) I love her.<br /><br /><b>My ONLY complaint was that it was, um, way too short.</b> The ending actually kind of felt a little “cheap” to me, because I don’t think it was very realistic (although I am still not very knowledgeable in these issues!!). The way it was left so open kind of irritated me—however, it also is one of the reasons this book is so touching?? It’s up to the readers’ interpretation of whether this case was really solved or not, and I love that. AND it’s amazing that the author can pack so much character development &amp; messages in such a short book!<br /><br /><b>This book was so, so important.</b> It’s as much as a must-read as The Hate U Give, and I hope that everyone will be able to pick it up one day! The characters are amazing, and the book raises so much awareness on topics and issues that are not being talked about as much as they should be today. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>The world is full of people who will always see me as inferior.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="18185479553088256869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2140782885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140782885" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2140782885?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=social-issues">social-issues</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2140782885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5820153660379749533">This is actually a book I would recommend teachers order for their schools to make their students read.<br/><br/>Because it doesn't simply tell a story; it introduces the reader to various important equality-related topics and values.<br/><br/>Note the word ''introduces''. It will not go into extreme length about, for instance, affirmative action, but it will talk about it in a way that makes the reader understand easily and then want to talk about it themselves by using their own examples.<br/> <br/>Martin Luther King is so</span>
  <span id="freeText5820153660379749533" style="display:none">This is actually a book I would recommend teachers order for their schools to make their students read.<br /><br />Because it doesn't simply tell a story; it introduces the reader to various important equality-related topics and values.<br /><br />Note the word ''introduces''. It will not go into extreme length about, for instance, affirmative action, but it will talk about it in a way that makes the reader understand easily and then want to talk about it themselves by using their own examples.<br /> <br />Martin Luther King is someone who is mentioned at least once by every teacher you'll encounter, especially your Humanities ones. Not to be confused with Martin Luther, who is a very different historical figure. Although they are both heroes, if I do say so myself.<br /><br />But the reason Doctor King is such an important topic, still today, is because of his decision to fight injustice with love and peace. Kill them unjust laws with kindness. Our main character, Justyce, studies Doctor King in order to understand his own life better.<br /><br />But it isn't always easy to keep one's anger in control and show a smile when it seems that there is nothing worth fighting for anymore. What's the point, if nothing ever changes? So Justyce has a tumultuous journey in front of him.<br /><br />Be there with him. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5820153660379749533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2136115278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136115278" />
    <a title="Brandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice"><img alt="Brandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582594594p2/36348070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136115278?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136115278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15976951143201449678">I loved <i>Dear Martin</i>. This is a timely book that depressed, infuriated, and devastated me at various parts. <br/><br/><i>Dear Martin</i> is about Justyce, a 17 year old high school senior at a prep school in Atlanta who, over the duration of the story, finds himself being treated inappropriately and unfairly in certain situations due to being a young African-American man. The book is timely with the social injustice that continues to pervade the U.S. <br/><br/>Justyce is aiming for an Ivy League college, balancing school, </span>
  <span id="freeText15976951143201449678" style="display:none">I loved <i>Dear Martin</i>. This is a timely book that depressed, infuriated, and devastated me at various parts. <br /><br /><i>Dear Martin</i> is about Justyce, a 17 year old high school senior at a prep school in Atlanta who, over the duration of the story, finds himself being treated inappropriately and unfairly in certain situations due to being a young African-American man. The book is timely with the social injustice that continues to pervade the U.S. <br /><br />Justyce is aiming for an Ivy League college, balancing school, friendships, including his best friend Manny who plays a central role in the story, peer pressure, and crushes, so to throw these unfortunate incidents into the standard teenager mix is a lot - More than a 17 year old should have to deal with. To cope with what he’s facing, Justyce starts writing letters to Martin Luther King, Jr., wondering what Martin would do in the situations Justyce faces. <br /><br /><i>“You ever consider that maybe you not supposed to ‘fit’? People who make history rarely do.”</i><br /><br />This is a YA book and definitely read like one, particularly in Part One, mostly due to the language, however it was an interesting story, and moved at a good pace. The tension was building but I wasn’t sure what the story’s turning point would be, although I knew what it was as soon as I read it. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“The time is always right to do what is right”</i>
</b> is my personal favorite Martin Luther King, Jr. quote. <br /><br />While <i>Dear Martin</i> left me heartbroken over some things, I liked the ending and feel like the book is a good read for YAs and adults alike.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15976951143201449678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2154083517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2154083517" />
    <a title="Romie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33510193-romie"><img alt="Romie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579037929p2/33510193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2154083517?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romie" href="/user/show/33510193-romie">Romie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=favourites-2017">favourites-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=poc">poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2154083517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4254558539781712988">Such a small book, and yet so impactful.<br/><br/>Do you ever just start a book and think ‘Oh you, you’re going to be a favourite’? Because that’s exactly what I felt when I opened this book and read the first chapter. By the second I was crying, and smiling, laughing, and in so much pain.<br/><br/>This book is mostly about Justyce, a seventeen-year-old black boy, trying to understand where he stands in his own life, what is opinion on racial inequalities is, what does it mean for him to be black in this white supr</span>
  <span id="freeText4254558539781712988" style="display:none">Such a small book, and yet so impactful.<br /><br />Do you ever just start a book and think ‘Oh you, you’re going to be a favourite’? Because that’s exactly what I felt when I opened this book and read the first chapter. By the second I was crying, and smiling, laughing, and in so much pain.<br /><br />This book is mostly about Justyce, a seventeen-year-old black boy, trying to understand where he stands in his own life, what is opinion on racial inequalities is, what does it mean for him to be black in this white supremacist world. And it sucks. So much. Because he’s surrounded by these white ‘I don’t see colour’ dudes who think racial inequalities don’t exist anymore and can’t even realise they benefit of white privileges.<br /><br />Justyce is a complex character, he goes through such an important journey throughout this book : going from this ‘let’s do anything to be integrated’ kid to this ‘I’m done being someone I’m not’ one. And it’s so heartbreaking to witness this journey, because Justyce has to face such a harsh reality, it hurts him every single of it.<br /> The moment that really changes everything for him is when he’s handcuffed fore helping his drunk ex-girlfriend to sit in her car … and a cop assumes he’s carjacking. Because he’s black and wearing a hoodie. How fucked up is that? He’s automatically assumed threatening because of his skin colour, don’t tell me we’re all equals because that’s bullshit and you know it. Justyce knows it, every single people of colour me included know it, so why is it so hard for a huge number — if not the majority — of white people to understand there is an actual problem going on and it won’t get better until they start opening their eyes? I’m not sorry for being harsh in my words, because the really is harsher, and I’m not there to make racist people feel comfortable. None of us are.<br /><br />This book has a lot of extremely interesting side characters, and I have to admit my two favourites were SJ and Doc. SJ is this white Jewish girl, she’s so fierce and head-strong, she’s aware of her privileges and uses them to make this fucked up world a better place. Doc is a biracial teacher, and he gives the best advices, you could just write them all on post-its and put them on your walls because trust me you need them. But there is also this one character I didn’t expect to end up liking : Jared. Asshole Jared. Mr-I’m-better-than-you-because-I’m-white Jared. It’s interesting to see how something awful that happens in this book affects him for the better. But people of colour shouldn’t have to suffer for white people to open their eyes and start acting like decent people.<br /><br /><i>“You can’t change how other people think and act, but you’re in full control of <b>you</b>. When it comes down to it, the only question that matters is this: If nothing in the world ever changes, what type of man are <b>you</b> gonna be?”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4254558539781712988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2165532869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2165532869" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2165532869?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2165532869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9922268942141354553"><i>“You ever consider that maybe you not supposed to 'fit'? People who make history rarely do.”</i><br/><br/>Nic Stone has been on my radar for a long time so I'm glad I finally managed to pick up her bestselling debut novel. I really enjoyed it as it was a super quick read that didn't waste a word. Every page, every chapter grabbed my attention. I thought the characters were well-painted with only a small number of strokes. I couldn't help but feel as if the story was slightly fractured, only showing a few outt</span>
  <span id="freeText9922268942141354553" style="display:none"><i>“You ever consider that maybe you not supposed to 'fit'? People who make history rarely do.”</i><br /><br />Nic Stone has been on my radar for a long time so I'm glad I finally managed to pick up her bestselling debut novel. I really enjoyed it as it was a super quick read that didn't waste a word. Every page, every chapter grabbed my attention. I thought the characters were well-painted with only a small number of strokes. I couldn't help but feel as if the story was slightly fractured, only showing a few outtakes of the life it documents and retelling the gaps with a sentence or two, therefore swallowing moments that I would've liked to see more of. The story felt a little incomplete and failed to play all my emotional strings. Another thing that bugged me was the switching from dialogue in quotation marks to direct speech introduced by a name + colon in a single conversation and sometimes paragraph.<br /><br />Nevertheless, it's an impactful novel that should be required reading. I'd give three stars for the craft and five for its importance and power.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9922268942141354553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3400873311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9060644637606230745">Dear Martin was a pretty quick audiobook. I actually listened to it in one sitting since it’s only 4 hrs and 32 mins long.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Short BUT powerful.</b>
</i><br/><br/>As with THUG, the story and message was emotional, and captivating. It reflects the news we hear almost weekly here in the US. Black teenagers being killed, and police officers not being charged.<br/><br/>For me, these kind of books are a reminder that I've had it easy, compared to others.   <span id="freeText9060644637606230745" style="display:none">Dear Martin was a pretty quick audiobook. I actually listened to it in one sitting since it’s only 4 hrs and 32 mins long.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Short BUT powerful.</b>
</i><br /><br />As with THUG, the story and message was emotional, and captivating. It reflects the news we hear almost weekly here in the US. Black teenagers being killed, and police officers not being charged.<br /><br />For me, these kind of books are a reminder that I've had it easy, compared to others. I grew up White, and in Europe, and have never been judged and profiled because of the color of my skin. Now as an adult it's my duty to remind myself that stories like Dear Martin and THUG are actually based on real life. This is happening every year, multiple times a year. And I can never forget that.<br /><br />Dear Martin was full of moments that made me think, but also made me sad. The injustice and hopelessness was crushing at times.<br /><br />Overall I’m incredibly glad I finally picked this book up. Because the hype is REAL! And it’s another of these must read books, in particular when it comes to own-voices.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>About the Audiobook:</b>
</i><br /><br />The audiobook was really well done. It was a quick and easy listening experience, and definitely a medium I would recommend.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>last thoughts</b>
</i><br /><br />Now, although I enjoyed Dear Martin, it didn’t quite enthrall me as much as THUG did – nevertheless it’s a book I would recommend anytime, same as Felix Ever After and All Boys Aren’t Blue. These books are all somewhere in the same category, they teach us, remind us, and open our eyes of all the things that are still wrong in our society.<br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br /><a href="https://thebrowneyedbookworm.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more reviews and book recommendations on my blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebrowneyedbookworm/" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Bookstagram</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3645676197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3645676197" />
    <a title="Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70046142-elle"><img alt="Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548160841p2/70046142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3645676197?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle" href="/user/show/70046142-elle">Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3645676197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10687934483147005415">I really appreciate YA authors that write directly to their teenage audience. There’s been a bit of a blurring of the lines between Young Adult and Adult fiction over the years, and sometimes it feels like teenage readers, especially ones in their early teens, get left behind. Maybe it’s due to the reluctance by publishers to classify books as New Adult, but about half of YA book readers are adults. This is fine, but adult readers and reviewers need to understand that these works are not made sp</span>
  <span id="freeText10687934483147005415" style="display:none">I really appreciate YA authors that write directly to their teenage audience. There’s been a bit of a blurring of the lines between Young Adult and Adult fiction over the years, and sometimes it feels like teenage readers, especially ones in their early teens, get left behind. Maybe it’s due to the reluctance by publishers to classify books as New Adult, but about half of YA book readers are adults. This is fine, but adult readers and reviewers need to understand that these works are not made specifically for them, and should be able to acknowledge that before picking one up.<br /><br /><i>Dear Martin</i> is a book for high schoolers, whether they’re big readers or not, and meets them on their level. It’s not juvenile and it doesn’t talk down to them. It deals with serious issues and will probably be triggering or upsetting to many of them. But it also is easy to read and has characters who think and act like real, modern teenagers. It’s short, which, honestly, was my favorite characteristic for assigned readings in class. And like other more recent YA novels, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39280444.Speak" title="Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Speak</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075671.The_Hate_U_Give__The_Hate_U_Give___1_" title="The Hate U Give (The Hate U Give, #1) by Angie Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hate U Give</a>, I think it would be an excellent addition to a school’s book list. <br /><br />Justyce McAllister has a lot going for him. He’s successful academically, goes to a great school and has some really solid friends. He doesn’t cause trouble, even at times when he would have good reason to. But to some people he will always be seen as Black before anything else—as someone inherently threatening. The police officer who accosts him one night certainly does, and though Justyce survives the altercation, he’s forever changed.<br /><br /><i>Dear Martin</i> is a story specific to Justyce, but is one that we should all be familiar with by this point. Especially after everything that’s happened in the United States in 2020, but also because it’s been happening for decades. You can see it stretching back centuries if you want to look that far. The characters go through a lot, but nothing that’s even approaching improbable. What makes <i>Dear Martin</i> so affecting is how familiar it all feels. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to everybody who is willing. If you’re white especially, and this is not the type of book you’d normally reach for, I implore you to read something outside of your typical experience. It’s not just necessary for personal growth, but societal as well. There is no point of ‘wokeness’ that can be reached where we will no longer have to vigorously interrogate our own biases. Race or privilege doesn’t always have to be front-and-center in your reading, but there’s no such thing as a ‘color-blind’ society, so why expect our stories to be any different?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10687934483147005415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10049672-kales?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10049672-kales?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10049672-kales?shelf=racial-diversity">racial-diversity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10049672-kales?shelf=physical-book">physical-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2118281418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3975923082817532281">I very much appreciated the message of this book, however it wasn't executed well. I have read other books (ALL AMERICAN BOYS, THE HATE U GIVE) with similar subject matter that just did it better. <br/><br/>Yes, I read this book in a day but that was because it was only 210 pages. I struggle with trusting a YA book that's only 210 pages, cause that's short! Like THE GREAT GATSBY short and surprise, I didn't like THE GREAT GATSBY. I felt like there needed to be more. I read in the acknowledgements that Nic</span>
  <span id="freeText3975923082817532281" style="display:none">I very much appreciated the message of this book, however it wasn't executed well. I have read other books (ALL AMERICAN BOYS, THE HATE U GIVE) with similar subject matter that just did it better. <br /><br />Yes, I read this book in a day but that was because it was only 210 pages. I struggle with trusting a YA book that's only 210 pages, cause that's short! Like THE GREAT GATSBY short and surprise, I didn't like THE GREAT GATSBY. I felt like there needed to be more. I read in the acknowledgements that Nic Stone's editor helped her cut the book in half and I wish I could have read the other half.<br /><br />Additionally, the format was distracting and weird. The book began with a third person narrative, which, was odd. Not the narrative but the narrator. It was clearly a female narrator speaking about a male protagonist and it was jarring and not succinct. Then it would switch to the letters Jus was writing to MLK...great, cool, I can deal with those two structures. But THEN for no reason, it would go into script format. What?! Like, why? The worst was when it would go from narrative to script within the chapter but then there was dialog in the letters and those were neither...It had no point or purpose. The constant format switches were distracting from the actual book. I appreciate those stylized choices when they have a purpose or a meaning to the story, but this just felt lazy and was distracting.<br /><br />Finally, the writing itself was poor and boring at many points. It was bland and non-descriptive. There were points I wanted to explore, but were, instead, glazed over. Other points felt very preachy. The characters, especially in the debate scenes, appeared to be merely mouth pieces and not actual people. That was frustrating. A lot of the characters were 2D for me, especially Sarah-Jean and Doc. The only characters that had actual development were Jus and Jared, which was great. Their development was well portrayed but it wasn't enough for me. That was disappointing.<br /><br />Oh! And the book didn't pass the Bechtel test which was highly annoying. Sarah-Jean felt like her own type of manic-pixie girl which pissed me off. Like, does that girl have a flaw? No? Okay, cool. And the other girl, Melo, was represented as a "messed-up hoe" so...yay women. <br /><br />I will not deny that the message in this book is powerful and should be expressed and written about. This book has a very LOOKING FOR ALASKA feel in that there is a before and an after structure to it. I'll admit, when the big shock happened, I had to close the book and try not to cry for several minutes. I was stunned. It hit me hard. I appreciate that I got a window into a world that I--as a cis gender, straight, white woman--will never experience. It was not the best portrayal of this message. When compared to some of the other books about this same topic, it falls short. I would recommend other books before this one and yeah, that makes me sad. But it mainly has to do with the formatting and the writing itself. It has nothing to do with the message or the representation of racial issues in our world today. I respect and understand the need for stories like this, and I am happy that they are being published and wide-read. We need more of them. This one, though, it wasn't my favorite. I thought it could have been executed better.<br /><br />Conclusion: No</span>
  <a data-text-id="3975923082817532281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
